**English:**

## 150

### Pesach

In response to his question — regarding the custom among Jews that during the holiday of Pesach, a man and his household are together (and in his home) — and especially the head of the family. — In addition to the fact that it is extremely difficult to be *mehader* as one desires in matters of Pesach when one is in a different place. And the rest is understood.
[quotation](From a letter, 5726-7)[/quotation]

...Regarding his question about traveling here for a few weeks, while I do not see a necessity for this, since he writes that he has a source to cover the majority of the expenses, then why not? However, that the trip should be before Pesach and to celebrate the holiday of Pesach here, does not seem right to me, since the custom of Jewish men is to celebrate together with their household if at all possible. And since it was not essential until now, surely it does not matter if the trip is delayed by a few weeks...
[quotation](From a letter, 11 Shevat 5715)[/quotation]

I confirm receipt of your letter from Monday, in which you write about the highly important work of *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*, by learning with Jewish children and *Shabbos* gatherings. May *Hashem Yisbarach* help that it should be with great *hatzlacha* and in a manner of *mosif v'holech v'or* (increasing and going and shining). Especially since *chinuch* is a matter that yields fruits and the fruits of fruits, the importance of this is self-evident.
And this is also one of the hints of Pesach, to which we are now approaching,

## 151

when everything is about children, as it is written, "And you shall tell your son," etc., and as our Sages, of blessed memory, tell us, that *hem* (the children) *hikiru-hu* (recognized *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*) *techilah* (first) at the splitting of the sea.
With blessings for *hatzlacha* in all the above and for a *chag Pesach kasher v'sameach*.
[quotation](From a letter, 10 Nissan 5720)[/quotation]

B"H, 27 Nissan 5764
Brooklyn, N.Y.
To the participants in the eleventh annual luncheon of *Agudas N'shei U'bnos Chabad* in Cleveland, Ohio
May *Hashem* sustain them
Blessing and peace:
With pleasure I received the news about your upcoming luncheon on Sunday, the first day of *Rosh Chodesh* Iyar (30 Nissan), may it come upon us for good.
May *Hashem Yisbarach* help that this annual undertaking should be crowned with great *hatzlacha* in all respects.
Since the undertaking takes place at the conclusion of the month of Nissan, it is to be hoped that on this occasion, the significance of this *Chodesh HaGeulah* and the holiday of Pesach will be emphasized for all Jewish women, and especially for Chabad women, and specifically regarding *chinuch al taharas hakodesh*. For the entire foundation of (the *Seder* and of) the *Haggadah* with which the holiday of Pesach begins is the *mitzvah* in the Torah, "And you shall tell your son" — to tell and explain to the children the significance of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, also as a preparation for *Kabbalas HaTorah*, in order to reach the level of "they recognized Him first" as it was at the splitting of the sea, with which the holiday of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* concludes.
The *Seder* and the *Haggadah* of Pesach teach us that one must not despair

## 152

even of a *ben rasha* (a wicked son), and one must bring him to the *Seder* table as well. At the same time, one must not rely on the *ben chacham* (wise son) that he will grow up to be a good and *frum* Jew on his own. One must occupy oneself with all Jewish children, without exception.
This is actually one of the tasks of Chabad women everywhere: to support the institutions and activities that aim to elevate all Jewish children to the level of a *ben chacham*. In addition to the primary task of *N'shei U'bnos Chabad* — to bring as much light and *kedushah* of *ner mitzvah v'torah ohr* into their homes and into their surroundings.
With blessings for *hatzlacha* and good tidings.

...I enjoyed what you wrote about the *farbrengen* of *Shabbos Mevarchim*, and especially that you also visited the homes of *Anash*. And surely the matter was done in a way that the women were also satisfied, and regarding what was discussed at the *farbrengen* of *Acharon Shel Pesach*, that the *geulah* of Pesach came about through the will of the women in this, and as explained in the *Midrash* that the righteous women influenced their husbands, and likewise at *Kabbalas HaTorah*, which is a continuation of the holiday of Pesach, and this continuation also includes the days in between. The verse specifies, "Thus shall you say to the house of Yaakov," etc., and our Sages, of blessed memory, explain in *Shemos Rabbah* that *Hashem* commanded to receive the consent of the women for this, and afterwards, etc...
[quotation](From a letter, 4 Iyar, 5715)[/quotation]

## 153

B"H, Tuesday *Parshas Vayikra el Moshe*,
*Rosh* *Chodesh* Nissan, 5750
Brooklyn, N.Y.
To the sons and daughters of Yisrael
Wherever they may be
May *Hashem* sustain them
Peace and blessing!
As we stand on the day of *Rosh Chodesh* Nissan, the *Chodesh HaGeulah*, which *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* established as the first month of all the months of the year ("This month shall be for you the head of months; it is the first to you of the months of the year"), it is appropriate to reflect on the meaning and influence of the "Month of Redemption" in the daily life of a Jew throughout the entire year ("The head of months... of the year"), and especially for this year.
* * *
The beginning of the year is seemingly on the first day of the month of Tishrei — *Rosh Hashanah*. However, this is only according to the order of the creation of the world, as *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* created the world

## 154

and leads it "by way of nature," meaning in a way that from a superficial perspective, the leadership appears "natural," because *Elokus* is hidden and concealed within the garments of the nature of the world ("*Olam*" from the word *he'elem* [concealment], and similarly *Elokim* in *gematria* is "*hateva*" [nature]) — and every *Rosh Hashanah*, this natural divine leadership is renewed and strengthened.
And there is another divine leadership, "miraculous leadership," above nature, to the point that it breaks all the limitations of the nature of the world — and this leadership is connected with the month of Nissan (as is hinted in the name of the month — "*Nissan*" from the word *nes* [miracle]).
For this reason, too, this month is called by the name "Month of Redemption":
Simply, this is connected with *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, for by way of nature, as our Sages inform us, not even one single slave could have escaped from Mitzrayim, yet at *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, a great and mighty nation went out from there, with a high hand, more than six hundred thousand adult men (twenty years old and above), besides the young, and also women and children! But *Yetzias Mitzrayim* was through open miracles that *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* performed and showed, "He performed for our ancestors and for us all these miracles, He brought us out from slavery to freedom, etc." — and even before that, as a preparation for it — "Ten miracles were performed for our ancestors in Mitzrayim."
* * *

## 155

And more deeply: The connection of "miraculous leadership" to the "Month of Redemption" is not only in that the open miracles included (and the essence of them is) the departure from Mitzrayim simply, but also in that "miraculous leadership" is the internal content of "*Yetzias Mitzrayim*": "*Mitzrayim*" from the word *meitzarim u'gvulim* (limitations of nature), and "*Yetzias Mitzrayim*" means — a departure from all limitations. The innovation of miraculous divine leadership is — the revelation of *Elokus* in a manner completely above all the limitations ("*meitzarim u'gvulim*") of nature.
And just as this is regarding the entirety of Yisrael, so it is for each and every one of the children of Yisrael individually, that "*Yetzias Mitzrayim*" is the personal *geulah* from his own limitations of nature.
— This is the internal content of what is said, "When you bring the people out of Mitzrayim, you shall serve *Elokim* on this mountain": The perfection of "*ta'avdun*" (you shall serve) does not come only through the fulfillment of all the commandments of *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, both in "turn from evil" and in "do good," and not only in absolute dedication to the service of *Hashem* with all one's strength and in all matters — but more than that: "With all your might," above the limitations of natural human powers. For this reason, it was in the ability of each one to reach "you shall serve *Elokim* on this mountain" only after "when you bring the people out of Mitzrayim," specifically the divine revelation of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* contains the power of above nature to elevate and raise each one above the limitations of nature and bring him to the perfection of "you shall serve *Elokim*," which is the "redemption of Mitzrayim," the personal *geulah* of each one individually.
* * *
It is understood that the revelation of *Elokus* in "miraculous leadership," being completely above the boundaries of nature, cannot be absorbed all at once and entirely by the intellect and powers of man, which, however elevated they may be, are nevertheless limited within the boundaries of nature. In other words: even when one sees with physical eyes open divine miracles, it is nevertheless not absorbed and grasped by the powers and senses in a penetrating and exhaustive way, and the matter remains beyond us.
We find this content explicitly in the Torah, and indeed in connection with the miracles of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, which at the end of the fortieth year of their being in the desert, Moshe Rabbeinu said to the children of Yisrael:

## 156

"You have seen all that *Hashem* did before your eyes in the land of Mitzrayim to Pharaoh and to all his servants and to all his land... But *Hashem* has not given you a heart to know, and eyes to see, and ears to hear, until this day... forty years... And you came to this place... And you shall keep the words of this covenant and do them."
And this requires explanation: The verse itself emphasizes that the children of Yisrael saw with their eyes all the great wonders of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, and if so, how is it that they did not understand, did not see, and did not hear the miracles until the end of the forty years in the desert? — But here it speaks of such seeing, hearing, and recognition that will lead to "and you shall keep the words of this covenant and do them," a seeing, hearing, and recognition that encompasses and influences a person to keep the "words of the covenant" to the fullest extent (as Rashi says that "from here on, *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* will be strict" that it should be "and you shall keep the words of the covenant"),
to the point that the matter encompasses the person and penetrates him in all details — both in the heart (to know), both in the eyes (to see), and both in the ears (to hear), and this is also hinted at in that we find in the *Korban Pesach* (meaning even before they left Mitzrayim) that all parts of the *korban* are roasted together on the fire — "its head with its legs and its innards," and afterwards they eat the *korban*, at which time the *korban* becomes "blood and flesh like its flesh." Meaning — the full and perfect sacrifice to *Hashem* must encompass the entire person, and the eating of the *korban* must be during a continuous duration of one meal, "in one house," and for all the members of the house.
And for this, a one-time seeing, hearing, and recognition of the signs and wonders through simple senses was not enough, but rather a deep, internal, and prolonged soul-contemplation of the miraculous leadership of *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* is required, so that the supernatural divine revelation will be soaked, filled, and thoroughly penetrated in all parts of the person's reality, until he transports himself and rises above all his limitations of nature. For this, a duration of forty years was required, to learn and delve into this, as our Sages learn from the aforementioned verse that "a person does not stand on the mind of his teacher until forty years" (— a person does not grasp the mind of his teacher until forty years).

## 157

This also gives a deeper explanation as to why Moshe Rabbeinu said these things to the children of Yisrael only after they stood to enter the land of Yisrael, on the threshold of a new period in the fulfillment of Torah and *mitzvos* (in the land of Yisrael, the possibility was given to also fulfill the *mitzvos* dependent on the land, all the 613 *mitzvos*), this is because only at the end of the forty years in the desert, when the children of Yisrael merited a "heart to know, and eyes to see, and ears to hear" all the "great trials... the great signs and wonders" of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, were the conclusion and perfection of "*Yetzias Mitzrayim*" achieved, which lead to the keeping of the words of the covenant in a full and absolute manner.
* * *
The aforementioned matters have a special significance in this year:
We are "forty years" after the passing of the *Nasi* of our generation, *k"k mo"h Admur*, in whom one saw openly "miraculous leadership," supernatural, both in the physical sense and in the spiritual sense, one saw his supernatural *mesiras nefesh* in all areas of Torah and Yiddishkeit, as is well-known, and after forty years one reaches "stands on the mind of his teacher" — *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* gives a "heart to know, and eyes to see, and ears to hear," including and especially the miraculous leadership of the *Nasi* of our generation.
* * *

## 158

May it be the will that as we stand in the auspicious days of the month of Nissan in the year "*Hi Tihiyeh*" (It shall be), "a year of miracles," each one will merit to see tangibly in his own life the miraculous leadership of *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* up to "miracles of miracles."
Up to the merit of the primary miracle — the miracle of the true and complete *geulah* by *Mashiach Tzidkeinu*, in Nissan they were redeemed and in Nissan they are destined to be redeemed, at which time the miracles will be even greater in value and in a wonderful way than the miracles that were at *Yetzias Mitzrayim*. And as our Sages, of blessed memory, interpret: "As in the days of your departure from the land of Mitzrayim, I will show him wonders" — that even in relation to "the days of your departure from the land of Mitzrayim" they are "wonders."
And *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* fulfills the heartfelt prayer of every Jew and all Jews: "May my prayer come before You, incline Your ear to my cry" and brings the true and complete *geulah*,
and we enter immediately into the land of Yisrael — like the entry into the land of Yisrael the first time, which was immediately at the end of "forty years"
and all this — immediately and literally.
With respect and blessing for *hatzlacha* in all the above
And with the blessing of a *chag Pesach kasher v'sameach* and bearer of good news
Place of signature
[new_section]

## 159

B"H, Friday *Parshas Tzav*,
11 Nissan, *Nasi* for the sons of Asher, 5750
Brooklyn, N.Y.
To the sons and daughters of Yisrael
Wherever they may be
May *Hashem* sustain them
Peace and blessing!
In continuation of the previous letter, from the day of *Rosh Chodesh* Nissan, and in order to clarify more the fundamental point that was explained in it — that the "conclusion" of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* and its perfection were at the end of the forty years in the desert, when the children of Yisrael merited a "heart to know, and eyes to see, and ears to hear" all the "great trials... the great signs and wonders" of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, in a way that all this was absorbed and penetrated well and filled all parts of the person: both the heart (to know), both the eyes (to see), and both the ears (to hear),
— it is appropriate to delve more and understand in a more fundamental way the innovation in the "heart to know, and eyes to see, and ears to hear" as they were after forty years in relation to the knowledge, seeing, and hearing that were at the time of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*,
and that the contemplation should be in a way that the matter will find expression up to action in practice,

## 160

and that it should be — like all matters of good and *kedushah* — in a manner of "we elevate in *kedushah*."
* * *
Just as we see in the physical life of a person that the heart conveys vitality ("for the blood is the soul") to all the limbs (as the saying goes: "*Liba palig l'chulei shiyfei*" — the heart distributes to all the limbs) — so it is in the spiritual vitality of a Jew, that in accordance with the depth and strength of the feeling of the Jewish heart toward *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, to that extent the matter is expressed in the service of *Hashem* in all the "limbs," the powers of his soul.
As is known, there are two general levels in the "service of the heart" — the yearning of the Jewish heart toward *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, which is the source and root of the service of *Hashem*:
One level is that a Jew is drawn and desires to draw closer and closer to *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* with the feeling of his heart, and a more elevated level — "the inwardness of the (Jewish) heart," which is a "movement" and feeling of complete connection and *dveikus* with *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, the inwardness of the point of the heart that is completely connected and united with *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, more than a person is dependent and united in his life, in his source of life.
And as stated — "*Liba palig l'chulei shiyfei*": In accordance with the two types of levels in the heart is the change in the action of the heart in all the powers and limbs of the person in the three general matters mentioned: (heart) to know, (eyes) to see, (ears) to hear — a change between the influence in the regular way and the influence in the elevated and deep way of knowledge, seeing, and hearing, because they stem from the *dveikus* of the inwardness of the heart and therefore they are in a more elevated way.
* * *
(Heart) to know: There is an understanding in *Elokus* according to the intellect of the limited man which is called by the name "*Da'as*

## 161

*Tachton*" (lower knowledge), as the "lower" strives (from below to above) to understand *Elokus* (as much as a created being can grasp the knowledge of the Creator);
And there is a mode of "*Da'as*" — "*Da'as Elyon*" (higher knowledge) — which is a completely different type of knowledge, as the "higher" understands *Elokus*, and this is the "to know *Hashem*" as He is connected — in the language of the *Rambam* — to the "hidden matters," the divine matters that are concealed, which cannot be grasped by regular human intellect and only from the side of the internal connection of the Jewish soul with *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* (being a "part of *Elokah* from above, literally") is a Jew capable of reaching the more elevated understanding in *Elokus*;
(Eyes) to see: In seeing a thing, there is a huge difference between seeing it for the first time and contemplating it after a fundamental recognition of it and a contemplation of a long time in all its details, at which time it is a completely different "seeing."
The main difference is not that in one glance all the details of the thing are not absorbed and grasped — for as is known, the sense of sight has the quality to absorb and see the thing entirely in all its details, but rather that a seeing that comes after contemplation of the details of the thing is in a completely different fundamentalism and depth, it is a penetrating and deep contemplation that "grasps" the entire person, he is completely immersed and concentrated in the thing as if there is nothing else besides the thing he is seeing.
It is understood that then the thing is seen with all its details in a completely different light;
(Ears) to hear: There is "hearing" in general, and there is a soul-"hearing" which means deep and internal absorption, a "hearing" that penetrates and encompasses the entire essence of the listener — "Let my words enter your ears," and its influence is general and completely full until there is a hearing that touches

## 162

the entirety (and essence) of the person, and as the *halachic* ruling, "One who causes deafness must pay him the value of his entire body" (whoever caused deafness afterwards is obligated to pay him the value of his entire body).
* * *
This level of the inwardness of the heart is called by the name "*Eitan*," as *k"k Admur HaZaken* explains, and his words are:
"*Maskil l'Eitan HaEzrachi*, *Eitan* is the essence of the soul... a part of *Elokah* from above... and *Eitan* is the strength of the soul that comes into revelation in the power of *mesiras nefesh*, and *Eitan* is a term for old, not newly created... and this is *maskil*, which is the source that invents and reveals the intellect, behold *maskil* is only for *Eitan*, for *Eitan* has a *maskil*, that which through the power of the *maskil* is the *Ezrachi*, shining to all the powers and senses."
In simple words: "*Eitan*" is the essence of the soul, which is a part of *Elokah* from above. One of the meanings of "*Eitan*" is — strength and hardness, and the intention is to the strong power of the soul that is revealed in the essence of *mesiras nefesh* of each one of Yisrael to *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*,
the meaning of "*Eitan*" is also "old" — ancient, for the strength and power of the soul is not something newly created and added to it but this is the *Elokus* that is in the soul since always, being a "part of *Elokah* from above."

## 163

And this is "*Maskil l'Eitan HaEzrachi*": At the time that the level of "*Eitan*" in the soul shines and radiates in a Jew, the essence of the *Elokus* of a "part of *Elokah* from above," the matter brings elevation in his intellect — "*Maskil*": the source of the power of the intellect is revealed in him, to the point of being "*Ezrachi*" (from the word "*zricha*" [shining]), through the "power of the *maskil*" the "*Eitan*" shines in all the powers and senses.
* * *
May it be the will that as we stand after a period of forty years, and in the time of the month of Nissan, the *Chodesh HaGeulah*, and this in a "year of miracles",
each one will act and influence, to reveal within himself the "*Eitan*" in the soul, which is found in every Jew, which will influence up to thought and speech and action of daily life,
and speedily and soon we will merit that the "*Maskil l'Eitan HaEzrachi*" will be revealed in its fullness, to the point that the matter is said in the present and past tense — it has already been revealed and is already shining in each and every one and penetrating within his entire being,
and in this month of Nissan literally we will see the fulfillment of the promise of *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* as stated by the sweet singer of Yisrael: "I have made a covenant with My chosen one, I have sworn to David My servant," for "I have found David My servant" —
that *Mashiach Tzidkeinu* comes and redeems each one of Yisrael and all the children of Yisrael from the *galus*,
and each and every one blesses and thanks *Hashem*: "Blessed be *Hashem* forever, Amen and Amen," the "new song on our redemption and on the liberation of our soul."
And all this — immediately and literally.
With respect and blessing
And with the blessing of a *chag Pesach kasher v'sameach*
Place of signature
[new_section]

## 164

B.H., *Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh*
25 Adar, eve of the day of the 3rd on which it was doubled that it is good
*Parshas Vayikra el Moshe*,
5751. Brooklyn, N.Y.
To the sons and daughters of Yisrael
Wherever they may be
May *Hashem* sustain them
Peace and blessing!
As we come from the days of Purim — days of miracles that *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* showed "in those days at this time," and as we approach the holiday of Pesach — in which we celebrate the holiday of "the time of our freedom," and thank *Hashem* for the miracles and wonders that He showed at the time of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* —

## 165

this is the appropriate time to turn full attention to the miracles and wonders that occurred in these days of ours, in the days close to Purim of this year.
These were open miracles not only for the people of Yisrael but also for all the nations, to the point that "all the ends of the earth saw" — everyone saw the miracles that occurred in this period.
The miracles in the days of Mordechai and Esther, "in those days," were hidden, as is known, within the ways of nature. Only after connecting the beginning of the reign of Achashverosh with "in the third year of his reign," and with "in the seventh year of his reign," and with "the month of Nissan in the twelfth year of his reign," and with the feasts that Esther made for Achashverosh and Haman — when one connects all these events into one sequence and after one reveals through deep contemplation that all this is a continuation of one matter — then one recognizes in this the hand of *Hashem*.
And this is one of the reasons that in the entire *Megillah* (which is from the twenty-four holy books) the name of *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* is not mentioned (explicitly) — because even the miracle of Purim occurred in a manner of concealment of the face, as one of the interpretations of the verse "And I will surely hide My face on that day" — that the matters are directed to the miracle of Purim: a miracle that is clothed and hidden within nature.
In contrast, in the events that happened in the last months until (the middle of) the month of Adar, a great miracle occurred for the benefit of the children of Yisrael and for the benefit of the entire world, a miracle open to the eyes of all the nations.
* * *
According to the natural conditions of the world, it was expected that this would be not only a declaration of war and the like, but that the war would drag many nations into it and flare up to the point of

## 166

a world war, *r"l*; but in practice, above the way of nature, not only was a world war prevented, but even the war that broke out — subsided.
At a time when all the signs pointed that one should expect a difficult war and prepare a large and mighty army, equipped with many weapons and specifically the most advanced ones — behold, after all the preparations, as is customary to prepare for a long war that is supposed to last weeks and months — the victory came in practice within a very short time!
The victory was so wonderful that it prevented not only much bloodshed among the nations of the world (as was feared at first), but it even brought about that the enemy would release, and in a good way, part of the prisoners of war and even part of those who were captured in the past.
— We have a commandment and instruction in our Torah: "Do not open your mouth" — to guard against talk of "black bile" — and that from now on there will be only good tidings, in the good that is seen and revealed. —
Furthermore: those who know what is happening "behind the scenes" — who are aware of many classified details that do not reach publication — grasp more and more the wonders of the miracles and wonders in this time, in these days.
* * *
Throughout this year — for which Jews gave the name and sign: "*Hi Tihiyeh* a year of wonders I will show him," and even before that, at the end of the previous year, which was marked by Jews with the sign: "*Hi Tihiyeh*" "a year of miracles" —

## ספירת העומר

_Section: ספירת העומר_

**Hebrew:**

## 182

### ספירת העומר

בעונג קבלתי החוברת הראשונה, ויהי רצון שתהי' התחלה טובה, וככל הענינים של תורה וקדושה יהי' גם מפעל זה באופן של עלי' והתקדמות מחיל אל חיל.
והרי החוברת הוכנה והופיעה בזמן המתאים שבין פסח לעצרת, שבשני רגלים אלו הי' לנשי ובנות ישראל חלק בראש, כסיפור חז"ל אשר בזכות נשים צדקניות נגאלו אבותינו ממצרים, בשביל לקבל את התורה מסיני, וקודם שניתנה התורה נצטוה משה רבינו לדבר עם "בית יעקב" — אלו הנשים — תחילה, ואח"כ עם "בני ישראל" — אלו האנשים.
וימי הספירה שבין שני ימים טובים אלו הם ימי הקישור בין "זמן חירותנו" ל"זמן מתן תורתנו", ימי עלי' והתקדמות מחיל אל חיל, כאמור לעיל, כמרומז גם כן באופן הספירה. שכידוע, אופן הספירה הוא לא במספר סידורי (היום יום שני שלישי וכו') אלא במספר יסודי — היום שני ימים, שלשה ימים, וכו'. שבמספר סידורי לא מודגש ענין ההוספה וההשתלמות אלא הסדר בזמן, מה שאין כן כשאומרים "היום שני ימים" ו"שלשה ימים" וכו' שמדגיש שהיום שבו עומדים משלים ומעלה ומוסיף על הימים הקודמים ועד לתכלית השלימות. וכמרומז גם כן בפרשת השבוע — "וספרת לך שבע שבתות שנים, שבע שנים שבע פעמים" וגו'. וכמו שהוא בשנים כן הוא בימים בכל שנה בימי הספירה שבין פסח לשבועות. ומספר שבעה בכלל הוא סימן לשלימות, כמרומז בשירת חנה — "עקרה ילדה שבעה" (בשלילת ההיפך מזה, כהדגשת הפסוק "רבת בנים" —).
ויהי רצון שכשם שהי' ביציאת מצרים — בזכות נשים צדקניות, כנ"ל, כן יהי' גם עכשו בימי ההכנה לקיום היעוד "כימי צאתך מארץ מצרים אראנו נפלאות" וכסיום שירת חנה — "ה' יחתו מריביו גו' וירם קרן משיחו" בקרוב ממש.
בברכה להצלחה ולבשורות טובות.
[quotation](ממכתב כ"ב אייר תשכ"ו)[/quotation]
[new\_section]

## 183

הערות לכללות הספר[ftnref\_1282\_\*].
אופן הצעת הענינים בספר הוא — כאלו כבר נמצא הקורא "בעובי הקורה", של בעיא זו, אלא שזקוק הוא לשקו"ט כדי לברר המסקנא, לתרץ הסתירות וכו'.
מובן, אשר רק יחידי סגולה הם בעלי ידיעה כזו. וגם הם — הרי כעבור זמן קצר לא ישארו בזכרונם כל הפרטים הדרושים להבנת הענינים.
וכדאי ונכון ביותר, שיבוא בתחלת הספר מבוא, בו תבואר השאלה (שלרובא דרובא של בני תורה — עצם מציאות השאלה יהיה חידוש היותר מפתיע שבספר) וגם הנקודות העקריות של שיטות השונות בפתרונה,
אשר עי"ז יורחב חוג מביני הענינים במדה גדולה.
יש לבאר בהקדמה או במבוא, או עכ"פ להעיר ע"ז, שהדיון בגוף השאלה עקרו נמצא (ומתחיל) ברביע האחרון של הספר. — אם לא היו קישוים בדבר, כדאי הי' לשנות את זה, כדי להקל, עד כמה שאפשר, התפיסא של היקף הדברים והבנתם.
ואפריון נמטי', על אשר מביא במילואם דברי המחברים עליהם דן, מבלי שיצטרכו לחפש בספרים עצמם.
בטח יגיהו הפרופס עוד הפעם, כי נלקו בחסר ויתיר וכו'.
\* \* \*
במש"כ אשר ע"י שיעבור את קו התאריך ברגע דנשיק עש"ק ושבת ויעשה זה איזה פעמים, הרי יבוטל אצלו האות דשבת. וזה א"א —
צ"ע מאי נפ"מ אם יהי' ז' ימים בלא שבת, או ז' מאות ימים בלא שבת. ולמה זה א"א — (ובפרט לדעת הרמב"ן — שמות כ, ח — שבכל יום ישנה המצוה זכור את יוה"ש. אף שגם לדעתו אין זכירה זו אות גמור, שהרי מחויב בתפילין).
ופשיטא שאין לאסור העברה זו ולדמותה לזה שדוחין מילה בכדי שלא לחלל את השבת אח"כ במכשירין (להרז"ה ולרשב"א — הובא בר"ן לשבת קלד, ב), או להאיסור לצאת בשיירא אם יבוא אח"כ לחלול שבת. ועיין ג"כ רש"י סוכה כה, ב ד"ה שחל: העוסק במצוה פטור כו' — כי בכל אלו ישנו החיוב אלא שסיבה דוחה אותו או מתירו משא"כ בנדו"ד.
וקצת דמיון יש למנחות (מא, א) טצדקי למיפטר נפשך כו'. ועיי"ש בתוס' ובהגמ"יי סוף הל' ציצית.
ועיין ג"כ שו"ת צ"צ חיו"ד סצ"ב. צפנת פענח מהד"ת פז, סע"ד.

## 184

ובכ"ז אינו דומה, שבכהנ"ל ישנה המצוה במציאות עכ"פ, אבל — אין שבת ביום הששי או ביום הראשון.
שוב ראיתי מה שציין בספרו למשנה ברורה.
\* \* \*
במש"כ בהנ"ל שאפשר שכל בנ"י יעברו קו התאריך בזמן הנ"ל ויבטל שבת זה לגמרי
— ולהעיר ממכילתא ר"פ תשא, שמדייק: הרי הגוים שהקיפו את אר"י וחללו ישראל כו'. ובמש"כ בזה צפנת פענח להגאון מרגצוב (ואין הספר עתה תח"י) שמפרש אשר דוקא בכה"ג שבטלה שבת לגמרי צריך קרא (שרק עפ"ז מובן שנקט במכילתא מציאות רחוקה כ"כ)[ftnref\_1283\_\*]. כן צ"ע בכגון דא — אם הניחו ישראל תפלין ביוהכ"פ של שנת גמר בנין ביהמ"ק, כיון שאכלו ושתו בו (מו"ק ט, א). ועיין צ"צ על מו"ק (פ"ג מ"ד) אשר האות הוא איסור מלאכה, ואפשר שגם ביוהכ"פ זה מלאכה לא עשו בו (לבד הכהנים מקריבי הקרבנות. ואולי גם המבשלים וכו' (אבל לא כל ישראל) מלאכת אוכל נפש?) ואכ"מ. —
אבל מציאות זו שכל ישראל יעברו בב"א קו התאריך אי אפשרית היא, עפמש"כ בסהמ"צ להרמב"ם מ"ע קנג, אשר חלילה לא­ל מעשות זאת כי הוא הבטיח כו'. — בצפנת פענח הל' קדה"ח ספ"ה הראה מקור לזה מב"ב קטו, ב והוריות ו, ב. וצ"ע כוונתו, דהרי גם אם ימצאו בני אפרים ומנשה בקצוי תבל הנה ארץ נחלתם לעולם עומדת, וא"כ לא כליא שבטא.
\* \* \*
מש"כ ליישב דברי החזו"א בפירוש דעת הרז"ה וכו', ובמסקנתו בשאלת קו התאריך, ונכנס בדיחוקים עצומים ואעפ"כ לא העלה תרופה, וכמו שכותב בכ"מ בספרו...
בסברת גרירה — אף שנמצאה דוגמא רחוקה לזה מהמקדיש אבר שהנשמה תלוי' בו. ודוגמא יותר קרובה בהל' עירובין שמשנכנס בתחום ובעיר — כל העיר כד' אמות וכו' — הנה בענין תחלת היום פשוט לד"ה שתלוי בשקיעה וזריחה, היינו שכל נקודה ונקודה היא בפ"ע בהחלט.
ומבהיל את השכל לומר ולחדש — שבמנין ימים אלו הנה אלפי מילין יהיו נגררים אחרי נקודה אחת.
\* \* \*
לכאורה התמי' הכי גדולה בשיטת הרז"ה היא, כיון שלדעתו קו התאריך הוא

## 185

בין ירושלים ומקום יושבי קצה המזרח, ומרז"ל לדידן לדידהו (ר"ה כ, ב) מפרש על שתי נקודות אלו, היינו שהי' ישוב בנ"י בקצה המזרח בזמן מרז"ל זה, א"כ איך לא נמצא בש"ס אף פס"ד אחד בהמון השאלות הקשורות עם קו התאריך? ועכצ"ל אשר אף שמפרש לדידן — בבל, בכ"ז לא הי' שם אף אחד מבנ"י.
מש"כ והעתיק מכמה ספרים ע"ד ענין קדוש שויו"ט למעלה, אחרי שלמטה חלוקים המקומות — יעוין ג"כ שו"ע רבנו הזקן או"ח ס"א סע"ח. וס' תורת חיים ס"פ בשלח ע' תש"ח ואילך.

**English:**

## 182

### Sefiras HaOmer

I received the first booklet with pleasure, and it is my prayer that it serves as a good beginning. May this project, like all matters of Torah and holiness, be one of ascent and progress, "from strength to strength."

This booklet was prepared and published at the appropriate time between Pesach and Atzeres. In both of these festivals, the women and daughters of Israel had a primary role, as the Sages relate that it was in the merit of the righteous women that our forefathers were redeemed from Egypt, in order to receive the Torah at Sinai. Before the Torah was given, Moshe Rabbeinu was commanded to speak first to the "House of Yaakov"—these are the women—and only afterward to the "Children of Israel"—these are the men.

The days of Sefirah between these two festivals are days of connection between "the time of our freedom" and "the time of the giving of our Torah"—days of ascent and progress from strength to strength, as mentioned above. This is also hinted at in the manner of counting. As is known, the counting is not done with ordinal numbers (the first day, the second day, etc.), but with cardinal numbers—"today is two days," "three days," and so on. In an ordinal count, the emphasis is on the order in time rather than the aspect of addition and perfection. Conversely, when we say "today is two days" and "three days," it emphasizes that the day in which one stands completes, elevates, and adds to the previous days, leading toward the ultimate perfection. This is also hinted at in the weekly parsha: "And you shall count for yourselves seven weeks of years, seven years seven times," etc. Just as it is with years, so it is with the days of every year during the days of Sefirah between Pesach and Shavuos. The number seven in general is a sign of perfection, as hinted at in the Song of Chana: "The barren woman has borne seven" (in negation of the opposite, as emphasized by the verse, "she who had many children").

May it be that just as it was at the exodus from Egypt—in the merit of the righteous women, as mentioned—so too it will be now, in the days of preparation for the fulfillment of the promise, "As in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders," and as the conclusion of the Song of Chana: "Hashem will shatter His adversaries... and He will exalt the horn of His Moshiach," very soon.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

(From a letter, 22 Iyar 5726)

---

## 183

Notes regarding the book as a whole.

The manner in which the subjects are presented in the book assumes that the reader is already "in the thick of the issue," and merely requires a discussion to clarify the conclusion, resolve contradictions, and so on.

It is understood that only a select few possess such knowledge. And even they, after a short time, will not retain in their memory all the details necessary to understand the matters.

It would be most worthwhile and appropriate to include an introduction at the beginning of the book, in which the question is explained (for the vast majority of Torah scholars, the very existence of the question will be the most surprising innovation in the book), as well as the main points of the various approaches to its resolution. This would greatly expand the circle of those who understand the subject matter.

One should explain in the preface or introduction, or at least note, that the discussion of the core of the question is found (and begins) in the final quarter of the book. If there were no difficulties in doing so, it would be worthwhile to change this, in order to facilitate, as much as possible, the grasp and understanding of the scope of the material.

And I offer my gratitude for the fact that you bring the words of the authors being discussed in their entirety, so that there is no need to search for the books themselves.

Surely you will proofread the draft once more, as there are missing and extra letters, etc.

* * *

Regarding what you wrote, that by crossing the International Date Line at the moment of *neshik* (kissing/conjunction) on Erev Shabbos and Shabbos, and doing this several times, the "sign" of Shabbos would be nullified for him—and that this is impossible:

It requires study: what is the practical difference if there are seven days without Shabbos, or seven hundred days without Shabbos? And why is this impossible? (Especially according to the Ramban—Shemos 20:8—that the mitzvah to "remember the day of Shabbos" applies every day. Although even according to him, this remembrance is not a complete "sign," as one is still obligated in tefillin).

It is obvious that one should not prohibit this crossing by comparing it to the case where we postpone a *bris milah* so as not to desecrate the Shabbos later with the necessary preparations (according to the RZ"H and the Rashba—cited in the Ran to Shabbos 134b), or the prohibition against departing on a caravan if it will lead to desecrating the Shabbos later. See also Rashi, Sukkah 25b, s.v. *Shechal*: "One who is engaged in a mitzvah is exempt, etc." For in all these cases, the obligation exists, but a cause pushes it aside or permits it, which is not the case in the matter at hand.

There is a slight similarity to Menachos (41a), "a trick to exempt oneself, etc." See there in Tosafos and in the Hagahos Maimoniyos at the end of Hilchos Tzitzis.

See also Responsa Tzemach Tzedek, Yoreh Deah 92; Tzafnas Paneach, Mahadura Tinyana 87, bottom of page 4.

---

## 184

And yet, it is not the same, for in the aforementioned cases the mitzvah exists in reality, whereas here—there is no Shabbos on the sixth day or the first day.

I have since seen what you noted in your book regarding the Mishnah Berurah.

* * *

Regarding what you wrote above, that it is possible that all of Bnei Yisrael could cross the Date Line at the aforementioned time and this Shabbos would be nullified entirely:

One should note the Mechilta at the beginning of Parshas Tisa, which infers: "Behold the nations that surrounded Eretz Yisrael and the Jews desecrated, etc." Regarding what the Tzafnas Paneach of the Rogatchover Gaon wrote on this (and the book is not currently at hand), he explains that it is specifically in such a case, where Shabbos is nullified entirely, that a verse is needed (for only according to this can it be understood why the Mechilta cited such a remote possibility).

Likewise, it requires study in such a case: did the Jews put on tefillin on the Yom Kippur of the year the Beis Hamikdash was completed, given that they ate and drank on it (Moed Katan 9a)? See the Tzemach Tzedek on Moed Katan (Chapter 3, Mishnah 4) that the "sign" is the prohibition of work, and it is possible that even on that Yom Kippur, they did not perform work (except for the Kohanim offering the sacrifices. And perhaps also those cooking, etc. (but not all of Israel) the work of preparing food?). But this is not the place to elaborate.

However, this situation where all of Israel would cross the Date Line at once is impossible, according to what is written in the Sefer Hamitzvos of the Rambam, Mitzvah 153, that Hashem forbid, for He promised, etc. In Tzafnas Paneach, Hilchos Kiddush Hachodesh, end of Chapter 5, he shows a source for this from Bava Basra 115b and Horayos 6b. His intent requires study, for even if the tribes of Ephraim and Menashe are found at the ends of the earth, the land of their inheritance stands forever, and thus "the tribe will not be destroyed."

* * *

Regarding what you wrote to resolve the words of the Chazon Ish in his interpretation of the opinion of the RZ"H, etc., and his conclusion on the question of the Date Line—you entered into immense complexities, and yet you did not provide a remedy, as you write in several places in your book...

Regarding the logic of "dragging" (that one location dictates the time for another)—although a remote example is found for this from one who sanctifies a limb upon which the soul depends, and a closer example in Hilchos Eiruvin, where once one enters the boundary and the city, the entire city is like four amos, etc.—regarding the beginning of the day, it is simple for all opinions that it depends on sunset and sunrise; meaning that every single point is absolutely independent.

It is mind-boggling to say and innovate that in the counting of these days, thousands of miles would be "dragged" after a single point.

* * *

Seemingly, the greatest difficulty in the opinion of the RZ"H is that since, according to him, the Date Line is

---

## 185

between Jerusalem and the location of those living at the edge of the East, and "from our Sages to us, to them" (Rosh Hashanah 20b) is interpreted as referring to these two points—meaning that there was a Jewish settlement at the edge of the East at the time of our Sages—if so, how is it that not a single legal ruling is found in the Shas regarding the multitude of questions connected to the Date Line? We must conclude that even though he interprets it as "to us"—Bavel—there was not a single Jew there.

Regarding what you wrote and copied from several books about the matter of the holiness of Shabbos and Yom Tov above, after the places below are divided—see also the Shulchan Aruch of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Orach Chaim 61, section 8. And the book Toras Chaim, beginning of Parshas Beshalach, page 758 and onwards.

(From a letter, 5715?)

---


## שמיני

_Section: שמיני_

**Hebrew:**

## 185

### שמיני

לאחרי הפסק ארוך נתקבל מכתבם מכ"ה וכ"ז ניסן עם המצורף אליו.
ויהי רצון שיוסיפו כהנה וכהנה[ftnref\_1284\_\*] בפעולות הקדושות — הפצת המעינות חוצה בתוככי הפצת היהדות בכלל, ומתוך שמחה וטוב לבב, שגם זה יוסיף במרץ והפצת הפעולות, וכן, מתאים להקריאה דשבת העבר מברכין חדש זיו, דמיני' מתברכין כל יומי דשבוע זה, אשר יעשה כאו"א הדבר אשר צוה ה' וכמבואר בספרא פ' שמיני ט' ו': אותו יצר הרע העבירו מלבכם ותהיו כולכם וכו' עשיתם כן וירא אליכם כבוד ה'.
בברכה לבשו"ט ולהצלחה בעבוה"ק,
[quotation](ממכתב א' אייר תש"כ)[/quotation]
[new\_section]

**English:**

## 185

### Shemini

After a long interval, your letter from the 25th and 26th of Nissan, along with its enclosure, has been received.

May it be the will of Hashem that you continue to increase, and increase even further, in your holy activities—the dissemination of the wellsprings of Chassidus outward, within the broader context of disseminating Yiddishkeit as a whole. May this be done with joy and a glad heart, for this, too, will add vigor and further the reach of your activities. This is also in keeping with the reading from this past Shabbos, *Mevarchin* for the month of Iyar—the month of *Ziv*—from which all the days of the week are blessed. May each and every one of you do that which Hashem has commanded, as explained in the Sifra, Parshas Shemini 9:6: "Remove that evil inclination from your hearts, and you shall all be... [one group to serve Hashem]. If you have done so, the glory of Hashem will appear to you."

With blessings for good tidings and for success in your holy work,

(From a letter dated 1st of Iyar, 5720)

---


## תזריע

_Section: תזריע_

**Hebrew:**

## 186

### תזריע

... זמן קריאת שם לבת — שמענו הוראת כ"ק מו"ח אדמו"ר, ע"פ מעשה רב של אדהאמ"צ לעשות הנ"ל בקרה"ת היותר סמוך. מנהגים שונים בזה ראה בס' טעמי המנהגים ח"ד עח. בס' כתר שם טוב להרב גאגין ח"א.
[quotation](ממכתב ד' מ"ח, תשי"ז) [/quotation]
[new\_section]
... ובמ"ש אודות נתוח של הצנורות — לא נראה לי זה כלל וכלל, והרי זהו שולל אפשריות הריון כמעט לתמיד. ובמה שמזכיר עצות אחרות, כנראה כוונתו למנוע הריון, עליו לשאול דעת רב מורה הוראה ויפרט לפניו דברי הרופא בזה.
אבל להעיר שלפעמים תכופות, אף שיש שקורים לזה התנגדות בדם, אין זה משפיע כלל על הנולדים. ועוד קורה, שלפני הלידה משתנה המצב לטוב וכו', והרי בנדון דידן, כיון שכותב שזוגתו תחי' יש לה קישוים כו' אפשר לבאר הענינים שכותב בזה, ולא בהדמים, והנפק"מ פשוטה, שע"י שתתחזק זוגת' בבריאותה, יש מקום לומר שיבטלו כל החששות שבענין.
והנה בכל ענין ובכל זמן נצטוינו להעלות בקדש להוסיף בעניני תורה ומצות ובפרט כשזקוקים לתוספת ברכה מנותן התורה ומצוה המצוה, ולכן מהנכון שהוא וזוגתו תחי' יוסיפו בהנ"ל מתאים למעמדם ומצבם, ובעיקר באתי לעוררו על ההכרח לקבוע לימוד בפנימיות התורה אשר בדורנו נתגלתה בתורת החסידות, שאם בכל הזמנים ובכל המקומות הי' הכרח בזה, עאכו"כ בתקופתנו ובמדינה זו.
מהנכון אשר יבדקו את התפילין שלו וכן את המזוזות בדירתם שתהיינה כולן כשרות כדין, וכן אשר זוגתו תחי' תשמור על מנהגן הטוב של בנות ישראל הכשרות, להפריש לצדקה קודם הדלקת הנרות בכל ערב שבת וערב יום טוב.
בברכה לבשו"ט בכל האמור.
[quotation](ממכתב י"ז תמוז תשי"ט)[/quotation]
[new\_section]

## 187

במענה למכתבו מיום 237, בו כותב אודות חוות דעת הרופא בהנוגע לזוגתו תחי' אשר כאילו אחד הצנורות סתום.
ובודאי ביאר להם הרופא מומחה, אשר ישנם שני צנורות ובאם רק אחד סתום, אפשר עבור ולידה ע"י צנור השני, ועוד זאת אשר ישנם אופני טפול לפתוח צנור סתום אפילו בלא נתוח, שלכן כדאי שישאל עוד הפעם דעת רופא מומחה בהאמור (טפול שלא על ידי נתוח) ויהי רצון שיצליח בזה.
ומובן שעליהם להוסיף בהנהגה טובה בחיי היום יומים מתאים להוראת תורתנו תורת חיים ובפרט זהירות ודיוק בעניני חוקי ודיני טהרת המשפחה (נדה, הפסק טהרה, טבילה במקוה כשרה דוקא וכו').
ומהנכון אשר יבדקו את התפילין שלו וכן את המזוזות בדירתם שתהיינה כולן כשרות כדין, וזוגתו תחי' תשמור על מנהגן הטוב של בנות ישראל הכשרות, להפריש לצדקה קודם הדלקת הנרות בכל ערב שבת וערב יום טוב.
וכשיכתוב שמותיהם בלשון הקדש (בצירוף שם האם שלו ושל זוגתו תחי') יזכירום על הציון הק' של כ"ק מו"ח אדמו"ר זצוקללה"ה נבג"מ זי"ע להנ"ל.
בברכה לבשו"ט בכל האמור. . .
[quotation](ממכתב כ"א תמוז תשי"ט)[/quotation]
[new\_section]
במענה למכתבם מט"ו סיון עם המוסגר בו והפ"נ שיקרא בעת רצון על הציון הק' של כ"ק מו"ח אדמו"ר זצוקלה"ה נבג"מ זי"ע.
בו כותב אודות מצב בריאות מרת. . . תחי', והנה כפי הנשמע כאן מהרופאים המומחים במקצוע דעניני נשים הם. . ולפלא שבכל מכתביהם לא הזכירו אם שאלו את הנ"ל. כן זכורני שהי' משך זמן שריפוי פצעים היו מנסים להחישו ע"י הנחה במקום הפצעים תחבושת מדברים המכילים וויטמינים ידועים הממהרים גידול הבשר והעור וכו', אפשר שבשנים האחרונים אין משתמשים בזה, אבל בכל אופן כדאי לשאול עד"ז.
במ"ש שמתאים להוראת הרופא נאלץ הבעל להשתמש בקונדס וכו' כיון שאין על האשה לעשות מה בדבר זה. — גם זה פלא, שאינם מזכירים אם שאלו דעת רב מורה הוראה בישראל בזה, ועוד שבאם יכיר הרב בכללות הדבר, הרי מהתרופות

## 188

הנעשים ע"י האשה, הוא לא רק השתמשות בחמרים כמיים, שאפשר בכגון דא אין יכולת להשתמש בהם, כי אם גם הענין דמוך, כיסוי מתאים במקום המתאים וכו' שלכאורה גם בנדון שלהם אפשרי להשתמש בזה כנ"ל באם יהי' היתר של הרב בכללות הענין...
בברכה לבשו"ט בכל האמור מתוך חוזק הבטחון בבורא העולם ומנהיגו והוספה בתורה ומצותי'.

ע"ד הרגיל ע"ע בפועל מכו"כ חדשים

## 189

בזמן המנחת יצחק — הי' כל התהליך באופן שונה לגמרי, וגם עתה משנים מזמן לזמן.
ת"ח שיודיענו תוצאות חקו"ד הנ"ל ועוד דוגמתם.
[quotation](ממענה עש"ק י"ז כסלו תש"נ)[/quotation]

... כותבים אשר בחנו רק ביצה אחת. ודעת רופא מומחה כאן, אשר באם ביצה השני' גדולה יותר וגם רכה יותר מזו שבחנו — כדאי לבחון גם אותה. באם דומה היא להראשונה — אין כדאי לבוחנה.
[quotation](ממכתב כ"ג סיון תשי"ט)[/quotation]

[new\_section]
במענה למכתבה מז' חשון, בו כותבת הצעת הרופאים בהנוגע לטפולים,
ומובן שבכגון דא מתחילים בהקל ופשוט יותר, ז.א. אמבטיות טבריא גרידא. ויהי רצון שיצליח הטפול במילואו, והשי"ת ימלא משאלות לבבם לזחו"ק בקרוב ממש.
וכאן מקום אתי להעיר, שבודאי זוכרים, שבהיותם כאן אמרתי וכפלתי לבעלה הרב שליט"א, שעליו להשגיח ולדייק יותר בעניני אכילה ושתי' ובכלל בבריאות הגוף, שנוסף על העיקר — שציווי תוה"ק הוא זה ובלשון הרמב"ם, היות הגוף בריא ושלם מדרכי השם הוא, הנה זה נוגע לענינם הפרטי לזחו"ק. על אתר ראיתי, שמתיחס הוא להענין באופן דמהיכי תיתי. ולכן כפלתי דברי ומאז חזרו לאה"ק ת"ו — מתגדל אצלי החשש שאפילו באופן דמהיכי תיתי אין בעלה הרב שי' משגיח על הנ"ל. ומובן שהשגחה בכזה — כוונתי פשוטה, שישאל אצל רופא סדר וזמני האכילה ומיני המאכלים בריאים וטובים, וכן בהנוגע לשאר הענינים הנוגעים בבריאות הגוף,

## 190

ויהי רצון שעכ"פ מכאן ולהבא יעשה האמור, ולו יהא בקבלת עול, ובלבד שיבוא הענין בפועל. ואין לך דבר העומד בפני רצון. ואם ירצה — יעשה.
מובן שכוונתי שתַראה מכתבי גם לבעלה הרב שי', ויהי רצון שיפעלו הדברים.
בברכה לבשו"ט בכל האמור.
[quotation](ממכתב יו"ד מ"ח תשי"ט)[/quotation]
[new\_section]
במענה על מכתבה מי"ח מר חשון, בו כותבת ע"ד מצב בריאות. . תחי':
הנה יש להודות להשי"ת שנתעברה, ולא להיות ח"ו במרה שחורה מזה, ובנוגע למיחושי', הנה, לכאורה, אם תהי' איזה שבועות באויר יותר מתאים לבריאותה — בטח ישתנה מצב בריאותה לטוב. ובודאי ישנם מקומות באה"ק ת"ו המתאימים לזה. מובן שצריכה לנהוג כמנהג בנות ישראל הכשרות בכל הענינים, ולבדוק את המזוזות בדירתה, ולפני הדלקת הנרות בעש"ק וערב יו"ט תתן איזה פרוטות לצדקה כשרה.
בטח שומרת הנ"ל הוראת הרופאים בעניני אכילה שתי' וטיול וכו', והשי"ת ימלא ימי הריונה בשלום, ותלד זחו"ק כשורה ובקל, ואחכה לבשו"ט.
[quotation](ממכתב אדר"ח כסלו תשי"ג)[/quotation]
מאשר הנני קבלת מכתבה — בלי הוראת זמן הכתיבה — וכבקשתה הנני עונה עליו מבלי לחכות על התור אפילו של מכתבים המהירים, ועל סדר מכתבה.
הנה פלא מה שמתחילה שכבה הניצוץ האחרון וכו' כי מאין לאדם ידיעות כאלו? וכנראה שכל יסודה הוא הגיל, ואין זה ראי' כלל, וכמבואר בדברי רז"ל

## 191

ורואים במוחש, שנשים שגילם גדול יותר משלה יולדות בנים ובנות ונוסף על זה הרי המסתכל בעולמו של הקב"ה רואה אשר מפני — בלשון הכתוב — רבו מעשיך ד' גדלו מעשיך ד' אי אפשר לאדם אחד להקיף ולהשיג את כל הענינים, וגם לא אפילו חלק חשוב מהם וגם לא אפילו רובם של הענינים הנמצאים בהד' אמות שלו ונוגע לחייו הפרטים ולכן נפרדו בני אדם למומחים במקצועות שונים, ואין האדם הישר מחווה דעת בהחלט אלא במקצוע שלו ובהאחרים סומך על המומחה בזה.
ובהנוגע לנדון דידן, הרי אף שהתורה מתחשבת עם חוות דעת רופאים ובחוות דעתם תלוי פסקים מיוחדים אשר בשולחן ערוך, ומהנהגתו של כל אחד ואחת הוא לעשות כהוראת הרופאים בהנוגע למעשה בפועל ממש, אבל ביחד ע"ז לדעת ברור בלבבו אשר השי"ת הוא הרופא כל בשר והוא המנהיג את עולמו כפשוטו היינו בחיי היום יומים של כל אחד ואחת ובפרט ובפרטי פרטים ועאכו"כ בענינים עיקרים.
כנראה מכתבה לא הי' בענין הנ"ל חוות דעת רופא מומחה, אבל באם גם הי' מקרה כזה אצל מי שהוא הרי המקרים שטועים הרופאים בכגון דא רבו מלספור, ואין הדבר תלוי אלא בחוזק בטחונו של האדם ובהתקשרותו עם בורא העולם (על ידי אורח חיים יום יום בבטחון שבמילא גורם לשמחה, וגם שמחת היכולת לפעול דבר מה בשביל הסביבה אשר גודל הזכות בזה אין לשער, וכידוע פתגם הבעל שם טוב, אשר נשמה יורדת למטה לעולם הזה למשך של 80-70 שנה בשביל לעשות טובה פעם אחת לישראל בגשמיות או ברוחניות, ומי כמוהו כהבעש"ט שהבין גודל הירידה של הנשמה מאיגרא רמה לבירא עמיקתא בביאת נשמה לעוה"ז ובכל זה אמר כנ"ל ומסר זה לדורותיו אחריו דורי בני הגלות ההולך וגובר, ובפרט כשהמדובר הוא באשה צעירה אשר עדיין לא נצלה כחותי' במילואם בהשפעה על סביבתה לעורר בהם את הטוב שבנפשם ולחזקו בטוב ואין טוב אלא תורה ומצוה, ולאו דוקא בימי השבת וימים נוראים ובמקרים יוצאים מן הכלל אלא בדוקא ובדיוק בחיי היום יומים אשר יש טועים לאמר שהם ימים אפורים), ובאמת אין נצרכה כל הסברה ואריכות לבאר נקודה פשוטה כזו ומספיקה רק מחשבה אחת אשר כל אחד ואחת מבני ישראל שהם מבני אברהם יצחק ויעקב הרי הוא חלק מהמחבר את הבורא והבריאה ע"י חייו כמו שהם, ובפרט ע"י פעולות הנ"ל וחיבור זה הוא תכלית כל הבריאה כולה.
בודאי למותר להוסיף אשר אין כוונתי בכל הנ"ל למעט ח"ו הענין דבן ובת ואיני בא אלא להראות על האמת המוחלט, שאין כל מקום לעצבות ועאכו"כ לביטוי שכותבת ליאוש ואדרבה ואדרבה.
בהנוגע לשאלתה אודות תחליפי הדירה והשנית והעיקרית לקחת ילד לתוך ביתם לחנכו, הרי זה תלוי בהשפעה שיהי' לזה עלי' ועל בעלה שי' ואם עי"ז יתוסף שמחה ותתחזק מדת בטחונה בהשי"ת אשר ימלא משאלותם לטובה בזחו"ק, בודאי נכון הדבר וכמדומה שכבר כתבתי להם פעם במכתבי מיוסד על אחת השיחות של

## 192

כ"ק מו"ח אדמו"ר אשר אף שמוכרח שהאדם יעשה חשבון בנפשו בכל זה מוכרח ג"כ שלא יהי' זה אלא בזמנים מיוחדים כי בלא"ה מרובה ההפסד על השכר, וכלך מעשיית חשבון הנפש בכל יום או אפילו פעם בשבוע, ומוטב אשר תשקיע כשרונותי' בפעולות טובות בהשפעה על סביבה, והקב"ה משלם מדה כנגד מדה אלא שכמה פעמים ככה.
בברכה לשמחה ולבשו"ט בכל הנ"ל.
[quotation](ממכתב כ"ח תשרי תשט"ו)[/quotation]
[new\_section]

**English:**

## 186

### Tazria

... Regarding the timing of naming a daughter — we have heard the instruction of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, based on the *maaseh rav* (established practice) of the Mitteler Rebbe, to perform this at the earliest possible Torah reading. For various customs regarding this, see the sefer *Taamei HaMinhagim*, Part 4, page 78, and the sefer *Kesser Shem Tov* by Rabbi Gagin, Part 1.
[From a letter of 4 MarCheshvan, 5717]

... Regarding what you wrote concerning the surgery on the fallopian tubes — this does not seem advisable to me at all, as it effectively precludes the possibility of pregnancy almost permanently. Regarding your mention of other methods, if you intend to prevent pregnancy, you must consult a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah* (halachic authority) and detail the doctor's findings to him.

However, I would like to point out that frequently, even when people call it a "blood incompatibility," it has no effect whatsoever on the children born. Furthermore, it often happens that the situation changes for the better before the birth, etc. In the present case, since you write that your wife, *tichyeh*, is experiencing difficulties, it is possible to explain the matters you describe in that light, rather than as a blood issue. The practical difference is simple: by your wife strengthening her health, there is room to say that all the concerns in this matter will be nullified.

In every situation and at all times, we are commanded to "ascend in holiness," to increase in matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, especially when one is in need of additional blessing from the Giver of the Torah and the Commander of the *mitzvos*. Therefore, it is appropriate that you and your wife, *tichyeh*, increase in these matters in a way that is suitable for your standing and situation. Primarily, I have come to awaken you to the necessity of establishing a regular study of *Pnimiyus HaTorah* (the inner dimension of Torah), which in our generation has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. If this was a necessity in all times and in all places, how much more so in our era and in this country.

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure they are all *kosher* according to the law. Furthermore, your wife, *tichyeh*, should observe the good custom of *kosher* daughters of Israel: to set aside money for *tzedakah* before lighting the candles every *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.
[From a letter of 17 Tammuz, 5719]

## 187

In response to your letter of the 23rd, in which you write regarding the doctor's opinion concerning your wife, *tichyeh*, that one of the tubes is supposedly blocked.

Surely the specialist doctor explained to you that there are two tubes, and if only one is blocked, pregnancy and birth are possible through the second tube. Furthermore, there are methods of treatment to open a blocked tube even without surgery. Therefore, it is worthwhile to consult a specialist doctor once again regarding the aforementioned (treatment without surgery). May it be His will that you succeed in this.

It is understood that you must increase in good conduct in your daily life, in accordance with the instruction of our Torah, the "Torah of Life," and especially in being careful and precise in the matters of the laws of *Taharas HaMishpacha* (*niddah*, *hefsek taharah*, immersion in a *kosher mikveh* specifically, etc.).

It is appropriate that you have your *tefillin* checked, as well as the *mezuzos* in your home, to ensure they are all *kosher* according to the law. Your wife, *tichyeh*, should observe the good custom of *kosher* daughters of Israel: to set aside money for *tzedakah* before lighting the candles every *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*.

When you write your names in *Lashon HaKodesh* (including your mother's name and your wife's mother's name), they will be mentioned at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the aforementioned.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.
[From a letter of 21 Tammuz, 5719]

In response to your letter of 15 Sivan, with the enclosure and the *pidyon nefesh* that will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe.

You write regarding the health condition of Mrs. ... *tichyeh*. From what is heard here from the specialist doctors in the field of gynecology, they are... It is puzzling that in all your letters you did not mention if you consulted the aforementioned. I also recall that there was a time when they would attempt to accelerate the healing of wounds by applying bandages containing certain vitamins to the site of the wound, which hasten the growth of flesh and skin, etc. It is possible that in recent years they do not use this, but in any case, it is worth asking about it.

Regarding what you wrote, that in accordance with the doctor's instructions the husband is forced to use a condom, etc., since the wife cannot do anything in this matter — this is also puzzling, as you do not mention if you asked the opinion of a Rav who is a *moreh hora'ah* in Israel regarding this. Furthermore, if the Rav understands the matter in its entirety, then among the remedies

## 188

that can be performed by the wife, it is not only the use of chemical substances — which perhaps in such a case cannot be used — but also the matter of a *moch* (a barrier), an appropriate covering in the appropriate place, etc. Seemingly, in your case as well, it is possible to use this, as mentioned above, if there is permission from the Rav regarding the matter as a whole...

With blessings for good tidings in all the above, with strength of trust in the Creator of the world and its Guide, and an increase in Torah and *mitzvos*.
[From a letter of 27 Sivan, 5718]

B"H
Before entering into the details of the *halachah*, you should clarify with experts who have been doing this for some time:
- Regarding the usual practice in practice for many months.
- How much time from the beginning of the process until its end.
- How many treatments are performed during this time.
- Sometimes more than one treatment is performed by one person, but not necessarily.
- In the meantime, the intervals — during which all the material is the responsibility of the warehouse keepers.
- How much material is added to the sperm.
- Their quality.
- Are there any materials among the aforementioned that are made from human sperm, and likewise regarding the women's ovulation.
- There are treatments that cause the woman to have the status of *niddah*.
- The husband's presence in the aforementioned — raises the question of *mesirut* (transfer/handling) in this.

## 189

At the time of the *Minchas Yitzchak* — the entire process was completely different, and even now they change it from time to time.
A *talmid chacham* should inform us of the results of the aforementioned inquiry and others like them.
[From a response of Erev Shabbos Kodesh, 17 Kislev, 5750]

... You write that they only examined one egg. The opinion of a specialist doctor here is that if the second egg is larger and also softer than the one they examined — it is worth examining it as well. If it is similar to the first one — it is not worth examining it.
[From a letter of 23 Sivan, 5719]

In response to her letter of 7 Cheshvan, in which she writes the doctors' proposal regarding treatments.

It is understood that in such cases one begins with the lighter and simpler option, i.e., merely the baths of Tiberias. May it be His will that the treatment succeeds in its entirety, and may the Almighty fulfill the desires of their hearts for *zera chaya vekayama* (living and enduring offspring) very soon.

Here is a place for me to note that surely you remember that when you were here, I said and repeated to her husband, the Rav, *shlita*, that he must be careful and precise in matters of eating and drinking and in general bodily health. In addition to the main point — that this is a command of our holy Torah, and in the words of the Rambam, that maintaining a healthy and sound body is among the ways of Hashem — it also concerns their private matter of *zera chaya vekayama*. On the spot, I saw that he relates to the matter with a "why should I" attitude. Therefore, I repeated my words, and since they returned to the Holy Land, *tizkeh lemitzvos*, the fear is growing in me that even in a "why should I" manner, her husband, the Rav, *shiy*, is not careful about the above. It is understood that by "care" in such a matter, I simply mean that he should ask a doctor about the schedule and times of eating and the types of healthy and good foods, and likewise regarding other matters concerning bodily health.

## 190

May it be His will that at least from now on he will do the above, even if it is by way of *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke), as long as the matter is brought into practice. There is nothing that stands before the will. If he wants — he will do it.

It is understood that I intend for you to show my letter also to her husband, the Rav, *shiy*. May it be His will that the words take effect.

With blessings for good tidings in all the above.
[From a letter of 10 MarCheshvan, 5719]

In response to her letter of 18 MarCheshvan, in which she writes about the health condition of ... *tichyeh*:

One must thank the Almighty that she has conceived, and not, Heaven forbid, be in a state of melancholy over this. Regarding her ailments, seemingly, if she were to spend a few weeks in a climate more suitable for her health — her health condition would surely change for the better. There are certainly places in the Holy Land, *tizkeh lemitzvos*, suitable for this. It is understood that she must conduct herself according to the custom of *kosher* daughters of Israel in all matters, and check the *mezuzos* in her home, and before lighting the candles on *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov* she should give a few coins to *kosher tzedakah*.

Surely she is keeping the aforementioned instruction of the doctors regarding matters of eating, drinking, and walking, etc. May the Almighty fill the days of her pregnancy in peace, and may she give birth to *zera chaya vekayama* properly and easily, and I will await good tidings.
[From a letter of Rosh Chodesh Kislev, 5713]

I acknowledge receipt of your letter — without the date of writing — and as per your request, I am answering it without waiting for the turn of even the urgent letters, and in the order of your letter.

It is puzzling that you begin by saying "the last spark has been extinguished," etc. Where does a person get such knowledge? It seems that the entire basis is age, and this is no proof at all, as explained in the words of our Sages,

## 191

and we see tangibly that women whose age is greater than hers give birth to sons and daughters. Furthermore, one who looks at the world of the Holy One, Blessed be He, sees that because — in the language of the verse — "How manifold are Your works, Hashem, how great are Your works, Hashem," it is impossible for one person to encompass and grasp all matters, nor even a significant part of them, nor even most of the matters found within his own four cubits that concern his private life. Therefore, people are divided into specialists in various fields, and an honest person does not express a definitive opinion except in his own field, and in others, he relies on the expert in that area.

Regarding the present case, although the Torah takes into account the opinions of doctors, and special rulings in the *Shulchan Aruch* depend on their opinions, and it is the conduct of every man and woman to act according to the doctors' instructions regarding actual practice, nevertheless, one must know clearly in one's heart that the Almighty is the "Healer of all flesh" and He is the One who guides His world literally — that is, in the daily life of every man and woman, specifically and in the finest details, and how much more so in major matters.

Apparently, your letter did not contain a specialist doctor's opinion on the aforementioned matter. But even if such a case occurred with someone, the instances where doctors are mistaken in such matters are too numerous to count. The matter depends only on the strength of a person's trust and his connection with the Creator of the world (through a daily lifestyle of trust, which naturally leads to joy, and also the joy of the ability to do something for one's surroundings, the greatness of the merit of which is immeasurable. As is known, the saying of the Baal Shem Tov, that a soul descends below to this world for a duration of 70-80 years just to do a favor for a fellow Jew once, whether in material or spiritual matters. And who is like the Baal Shem Tov, who understood the greatness of the soul's descent from a high mountain to a deep pit in the soul's arrival to this world, and despite all this, he said the above and transmitted this to the generations after him, the generations of the exile which is increasing, especially when it concerns a young woman who has not yet utilized her powers to their fullest in influencing her surroundings to awaken in them the good in their souls and to strengthen it in goodness — and there is no goodness but Torah and *mitzvos* — and not necessarily on the days of Shabbos and *Yamim Nora'im* and in exceptional cases, but specifically and precisely in daily life, which some mistakenly call "gray days"). In truth, no explanation or length is needed to explain such a simple point; one thought is sufficient: that every man and woman of the Jewish people, who are the children of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov, is a part that connects the Creator and the creation through their lives as they are, and especially through the aforementioned actions, and this connection is the purpose of the entire creation.

It is surely superfluous to add that I do not intend in all the above to minimize, Heaven forbid, the matter of a son or daughter; I only come to point to the absolute truth, that there is no place for sadness, and how much more so for the expression of despair that you write — on the contrary, and on the contrary.

Regarding your question about changing the apartment, and the second and main point of taking a child into your home to educate him — this depends on the influence this will have on you and your husband, *shiy*. If through this joy will be added and your level of trust in the Almighty will be strengthened, that He will fulfill your requests for the good with *zera chaya vekayama*, then the matter is certainly appropriate. I believe I already wrote to you once in my letter, based on one of the *sichos* of

## 192

my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that although it is necessary for a person to make a *cheshbon hanefesh* (self-reckoning) in all this, it is also necessary that it be only at special times, for otherwise the loss outweighs the gain. Desist from making a *cheshbon hanefesh* every day or even once a week; it is better that you invest your talents in good deeds by influencing your surroundings, and the Holy One, Blessed be He, repays measure for measure, but many times over.

With blessings for joy and good tidings in all the above.
[From a letter of 28 Tishrei, 5715]
